[DOB-255] - Admission (Discharged) in BAPTIST HEALTH CORBIN WOMENS HEALTH (continued)
Procedure Notes (continued)
URINE AM
TISSUE 
PATHOLOGY 
EXAM
Uterus, 
Cervix, R 
Fallopian 
Tube
Collected By: 
Gilbert, Travis 
Daniel, DO
11/5/2018 8:32
AM
 Procedure: The patient was taken to the operating room after informed written informed consent was obtained. She
was prepped and draped in the usual sterile fashion in the dorsal lithotomy position after general anesthesia was
obtained. We first placed in speculums anteriorly and posteriorly and grasped the cervix on each of the midline using
a toothed tenaculum. We hydrodissected circumferentially around the cervix and then made a circumferential incision
around the cervix. We then dissected anteriorly and posteriorly posteriorly we entered the cul-de-sac sharply and
placed a retractor. We then dissected anteriorly to the point where we got into the anterior cul-de-sac. Next we took
bites on each side using the Haney clamps, we then cut with scissors and suture ligated with 0 Vicryl. We held the
sutures for manipulation later on. Next using the LigaSure device we took serial bites on each side of the uterus
doubly cauterizing each pedicle and then cutting using the LigaSure. Once we got up to the fundus and the cornua we
doubly cauterized it and delivered the uterus. We were able to easily remove the right fallopian tube at the left
fallopian tube was little higher in the pelvis and we were on not able to reach it. We then attached the ipsilateral
uterosacral ligaments to the vaginal cuff angles bilaterally and then closed the remainder of the vaginal cuff using
interrupted 2-0 Vicryl stitches in a figure-of-eight fashion. Next we performed the TVT. We isolated the mid urethra between 2 Allis clamps made a 1 cm incision and dissected
out laterally and then retropubically. We then placed the TVT trocar through the incision and guided it retropubically
and lateral to the urethra we hugged the pubic bone the entire time as we guided it suprapubically. We brought it out
through the skin suprapubically. We did this bilaterally. Next we performed a cystourethroscopy making sure that we
had not injured the bladder with the TVT trochars and we did not. We then pulled the mesh through and tensioned it
loosely to where we could get a pair of Metzenbaum scissors under it easily. We irrigated it. We then closed this
incision using a running locking stitch of 2-0 Vicryl. All sponge lap and needle counts were correct there were no complications with the procedure. Findings: Uterine prolapse, normal bladder
Complications: none
Grafts or Implants: TVT Mesh
Travis Daniel Gilbert, DO
Date: 11/5/2018 Time: 9:03 AM
Electronically signed by Gilbert, Travis Daniel, DO at 11/05/18 0907
Printed on 1/19/23 12:43 PM Page 598

[DOB-347] - Admission (Discharged) in BAPTIST HEALTH CORBIN WOMENS HEALTH (continued)
Care Plan (continued)
Gently manipulate drain tubing to maintain patency when clots are present
Provide protective hemostasis
Prevent hypothermia which can alter clotting ability
Restrict nonessential activity with active bleeding
Anticipate the need for administration of volume expansion and fluid resuscitation (e.g., crystalloids, colloids, blood products) and possible procedure/surgery to control bleeding
Intervention: Promote Effective Bowel Elimination
Frequency: Per CPG
Dates: Start: 11/05/18
Description: Encourage hydration/advance oral intake as tolerated
Monitor abdominal girth/bowel sounds/flatus pattern
Assess for signs/symptoms of urinary retention
Advocate early removal of indwelling catheter
Encourage frequent voiding
Monitor urine color/characteristics
Monitor/record urine and stool output
Intervention: Monitor and Manage Pain
Frequency: Per CPG
Dates: Start: 11/05/18
Description: Use a consistent pain scale for regular/frequent assessment
Mutually determine/review pain management plan regularly
Consider the presence of pre-existing persistent pain
Recognize need to maintain chronic regimen with additional dosing to manage acute pain
Eliminate/minimize actual and potential painful stimuli
Use a multimodal approach (e.g., more than one type/route of medication)
Titrate medications to patient response
Anticipate need to manage drug-induced side effects
Intervention: Prevent or Manage Infection
Frequency: Per CPG
Dates: Start: 11/05/18
Description: Implement transmission-based precautions as appropriate
Minimize exposure/entry of organisms
Anticipate discontinuation of prophylactic antibiotic therapy 24 hours after surgery
Perform daily review of invasive device necessity; promptly remove unnecessary devices
Provide fever/comfort measures
Monitor for early signs of sepsis
Anticipate the need for fluid resuscitation/advanced support
Intervention: Prevent or Manage Nausea and Vomiting
Frequency: Per CPG
Dates: Start: 11/05/18
Description: Decrease environmental stimuli, create quiet/relaxed atmosphere
Reposition carefully (e.g., move/turn slowly)
Minimize use of opioid medication; consider alternatives
Consider complementary therapy (e.g., acupuncture point P6 stimulation, aromatherapy)
Maintain fluid/electrolyte balance; encourage oral fluids when able
Prophylactically administer prescribed antiemetic agents in patients with risk factors
Provide comfort measures
Provide aspiration prophylaxis
Intervention: Prevent and Manage VTE (venous thromboembolism) Risk
Frequency: Per CPG
Dates: Start: 11/05/18
Description: Assess for VTE risk
Encourage/assist with early ambulation
Initiate/maintain compression therapy
Encourage both active and passive leg exercises while in bed, if unable to ambulate
Intervention: Promote Surgical Wound Healing/Prevent Dehiscence

[DOB-353] - Admission (Discharged) in BAPTIST HEALTH CORBIN WOMENS HEALTH (continued)
Patient Education (continued)
Title: Retired Hysterectomy (Adult) ()
Topic: Retired Self-Management (Resolved)
Point: Retired VTE Prevention (Resolved)
To prevent VTE, early frequent ambulation is encouraged and should be continued at home.
If confined to a bed or wheelchair, a caregiver will need to assist with arm and leg movement. Provider’s instructions for continuing VTE prophylaxis medication should be followed at home. This can happen up to 3 months after your surgery.
If you have a blood clot, it will most likely be in one of your arms or legs. A blood clot can also travel to your lungs. This is known as a pulmonary embolism. One of the best things you can do to prevent a blood clot is to get up and walk as soon as possible and often.
If you are not able to get out of bed or you are in a wheelchair, your caregiver should help you move your arms and legs
often.
You may need to keep taking medicine to keep blood clots from forming after you go home as directed by your doctor. Point: Retired Pain Management (Resolved)
Medication should be taken before pain becomes too severe. Pain medication dosing and frequency should be followed as prescribed. The medicine should be taken just as the doctor tells you. Take pain medicine at a planned time so the pain will not get too bad. It can be hard to get comfortable again if you wait too
long.
Some pain medicines have more than one type of medicine in them. Taking pain medicine too soon or giving it with other
medicine may be harmful. This includes the medicine you buy on the shelf in the store. Point: Retired Provider Follow-Up (Resolved)
Point: Retired Activity (Resolved)
Description:
Following surgery, risk for developing VTE continues for up to 90 days. Patient Friendly Description:
Surgery increases the chance of a blood clot forming.
Learning Progress Summary
Description:
Managing pain is an important part of surgical healing. Patient Friendly Description:
Medicine will be ordered by the doctor to help treat your pain.
Learning Progress Summary
Description:
Encourage keeping follow-up appointments as they are an important part of recovery. Patient Friendly Description:
Keep all doctor appointments. The doctor will watch to make sure you are healing as expected. Learning Progress Summary

[DOB-355] - Admission (Discharged) in BAPTIST HEALTH CORBIN WOMENS HEALTH (continued)
Patient Education (continued)
Review post-discharge activity restrictions post-discharge which may include:
lifting
pushing/pulling
sports
driving
sexual activity
There may be limits set for:
bending over
lifting
pushing, pulling
playing sports, exercise
sexual activity
driving as applicable
Make sure that you do not do too much. This can cause you to become too tired to do recommended activity. Be sure to balance activity with rest. You may also follow a set bedtime and limit visitors. Try to do calm things like reading, watching TV and listening to music. Point: Retired Dressing/Incision Care (Resolved)
handwashing before and after touching dressing or incision
bathing considerations
incision cleansing, inspection and anticipated findings during healing
dressing change technique and frequency
care for skin surrounding surgical site
Keep incision area clean and dry. Follow the doctor's instructions for removing or changing bandages. Let any thin, white pieces of tape fall off on their own. Begin with sponge baths and only take showers when the doctor approves. Pat incision dry (do not rub). Do not take a bath or go swimming until the doctor tells you it is safe.
Description:
Balance activity with periods of rest during recovery. Patient Friendly Description:
Follow the doctor's instructions for activity.
Learning Progress Summary
Description:
Dressing/incision care should include:
Patient Friendly Description:
Always wash hands before touching any area around the surgery site.

symptoms become worse

feel worse
Point: Retired VTE Symptoms (Resolved)
Warning signs of a blood clot in your arm or leg are:
soreness in your arm or leg not from an injury
swelling of your arm or leg
your arm or leg is warm to touch
your arm or leg is red, pale or bluish in color
Warning signs of a blood clot in your lung are:
trouble breathing
pain in your chest that gets worse with a deep breath

The medical treatment rendered to the patient during this visit may be provided by independent practitioners. They
may or may not be employees or agents of the Hospital. These practitioners may include, but are not limited to:
surgeons, anesthesiologist(s), cardiologist(s), radiologist(s), pathologist(s), neurologist(s), emergency room
physician(s), physician assistant(s), certified registered nurse anesthetist(s) (CRNA) and other professionals. You
may be billed separately for the services of these practitioners or the bill you receive may include separate charges
for their services. These charges are established by the practitioners.
This section is to be completed by the licensed caregiver performing procedure.
RISKS, BENEFITS, & ALTERNATIVES- has explained to me: (1)the
nature of the proposed procedure; (2)the potential risks, benefits and side effects, including potential problems
that might occur during recuperation; (3}}he likelihood of achieving goals; (4) reasonable alternatives to the
procedure, if any; (5) the relevant be: and risks, and side effects associated with those alternatives, including
the possible results o {ec siving ¢treafnent. and services, likelihood of achieving goals and (6) possible
result of not receivifig care, \tr ¢ Bd pices. (6 | a
Physician’s signature Date (3 Time 7
BLOOD TRANSFUSION AND BLOOD PRODUCTS RISKS, BENEFITS, & ALTERNATIVES-If you wish not to
receive blood or blood products please request to sign a refusal form. 1) Some surgical procedures may
require blood transfusions or blood products. | was informed that | may need to have blood products administered
during the course of mytreatment. 2) It has been explained to me that the administration of blood products
involves the introduction of the product into one of myveins, commonly in the arm using a needie. | understand
that the amount of blood products administered is determined by my doctor based upon my particular needs. 3) It
has been explained to me that the administration of blood products may expose me to certain risks. Minor or
temporary reactions, such as slight bruising, swelling, or local infection of the area where the needle pierces the
skin is not uncommon. Non-serious reactions may include headache, fever, or a mild skin reaction, such as itching
or arash. Rare, but serious reactions are possible such as the transmission of diseases including hepatitis and
AIDS, which require lengthy treatment and can befatal. It has been further explained that while procedures for
screening blood products for diseases such as AIDS and hepatitis are effective, these procedures are not perfect
and there is a risk of exposure to AIDS, hepatitis, or other blood-borne disease. | have taken all of these risks into
consideration and have decided that the benefits of receiving blood products outweigh the risks. 4) | have been
made aware of the reasonably available alternatives to the administration of blood products and the risks and
benefits of those alternatives including autologous blood transfusion, directed donation and not having any blood
products administered. | understand that | may be able to donate one of several units of myown blood to be used
during planned elective surgery and that mydoctor must determine myability to donate for myself. This is called
autologous transfusion. If | choose to have an autologous transfusion, | understand that the last unit of blood must
be donated one week prior to expected use. | also understand that | may choose a directed donation. A directed
donation means |am allowed to select my own donors. There is no scientific evidence that directed donations are
safer but |understand many patients fee! more comfortable designating their own donors. The designated donor
can donate within thirty (30) days of the anticipated need for the blood. It takes at least seventy-two (72) hours for
a unit from a directed donor to be processed and available for transfusion. These arrangements must be made by
mydoctor.

TISSUE REMOVAL-| understand that this procedure(s) may result in the removal of body tissue or body parts. |
consent to their disposal according to the hospital policies and the recommendations of myphysician. Further, |
consent to the performance of operations and procedures in addition to or different from those named above which
myphysician deems necessary or advisable for mywell being because of presently unforeseen or changed
conditions or circumstances.
SALES REPRESENTATIVES-| understand that there may be a representative from a company that furnishes
equipment to surgeons and hospitals present in the room during my surgical procedure. | also understand that
his/her function is strictly to observe and advise, and that this person has no part in mydirect care.
NESTHESIA-| understand that this procedure may require anesthesia. An anesthesiologist has or will explain the
nesthesia alternatives. Complications from any type of anesthetic are infrequent, but do occur. Complications
are more frequent for patients in poor health than for patients in good health. Complications associated with all
types of anesthesia include temporary or permanent damage to teeth, lips, nose, throat, voice box, windpipe, eyes,
nerves, or blood vessels. Drug reaction may occur and may be minor or serious even requiring resuscitation.
Breathing problems may develop.
Headache, back pain, some degree of awareness, infection, nausea and/or vomiting may occur. There are some
very serious complications, which are uncommon, but can occur. These include paralysis, brain damage, or death.
There are other potential complications depending on your situation; however, it is not possible to advise you of
every imaginable complication. The purpose of this is not to frighten you, but to properly inform you. Serious
complications are unlikely. The benefits of surgery and anesthesia, except in extreme circumstances, outweigh
potential risks. | agree that the potential benefit of the procedure(s) outweighs the potential risks of anesthesia.
| understand that myprocedure is scheduled to be done with one of the following anesthesia marked below:
@General Anesthesia-monitoring and care provided bythe anesthesiologist with or without a CRNA
OMonitored Anesthesia Care-possible sedation, monitoring and care provided bythe anesthesiologist or a
CRNA
ORegional Anesthesia-monitoring and care provided by the anesthesiologist or a CRNA
OLocal Anesthesia-care managed bythe Physician and monitored by a registered nurse
OModerate Sedation-care managed by the Physician and monitored bya registered nurse
ONot applicable
|understand that | must be:
1.) Accompanied by a responsible adult.
2.) Not take public transportation without the presence of another adult.
3.) Not drive a car, ingest alcoholic beverages, or depressant medication without direct permission from the
physician, for a minimum of 24 hours.
4.) Not make any important decisions or sign any important documents or checks for 24 to 36 hours
There is the possibility that any of the services provided above may convert to a general anesthetic. These same
complications may occur with local anesthesia. It may become necessary for the anesthesiologist to render care in
a life-threatening emergency situation without myprevious consent. If during a local anesthetic an emergent
situation arises | understand that myphysician may consult with an anesthesiologist to render the necessary
emergency medical care. Byte U fe

UNDERSTANDING CONSENT- | have read, or had read to me, this consent form and | understand what | have
signed. | have had an opportunity to ask questions, all of which have been answered to mysatisfaction. | hereby
consent to the above-described surgical procedure(s) to be performed bythe above-referenced physician and any
assistants he or she may choose. | also consent to the administration of medications, including anesthesia, as my
physician and/or anesthesiologist determine advisable. |further consent to any procedures that become
necessary if complications occur. In addition, | authorize the staff of Baptist Regional Medical Center to render any
and all customary or necessary care in connection with this procedure(s). Please sign that you understand this
document.
Based on the explanation of the benefits and risks of this procedure and the alternatives available, |agree that the
potential benefits of theprocedure(s) outweigh the potential risks involved. It has been explained to me that all
surgical procedures involve some risk, including risks such as severe loss of blood, infection, cardiac arrest and,
in rare instances, death. It has been explained to me thatafirst assistant or one of the physicians in his/her group
may be involved in this procedure. |acknowledge that medicine is not an exact science and that noguarantees
have been made to me concerning the results of the procedure(s) described above. | understand that if
complications occur, additional medical treatment may be required and emergency medical treatment is available.

e To work together in providing your treatment in a respectful manner.
e To help you meet the goals of your treatment plan.
e To maintain a safe environment for thedelivery of health care services at our hospital.
e To protect the safety and well-being of all patients, visitors, staff and care providers.
We value you as a patient and want to continue to provide you with high quality safe care and service. To do so,
we need to outline the expectations that will foster an effective provider- patient relationship.
The following expectations are required to maintain an effective provider- patient relationship.
Patient Behavior Expectations
e | will comply with the medical treatment plan and recommendations developed between my provider
and me.
e | will treat my care providers with dignity and respect, and | expect to be treated with dignity and respect.
e | understand that profanity, physical or verbal abuse, or any other form of violence against anyone will
not be allowed or tolerated.
e | understand that unauthorized and/or illegal drugs are not allowed in the hospital.
e For my safety, |will not leave the nursing unit where |am a patient during my treatment unless
accompanied by hospital personnel for diagnostic procedures or treatments.
e If leave the unit, itwill be considered going against medical advice and | maybe discharged from the
hospital. For any future medical care, |would need to consult my primary care MD/Provider or go to an
Emergency Room for further evaluation. Hospital staff have the right not to re-admit me for further care
unless an emergency situation exists.

INPATIENT AND OUTPATIENT CONDITIONS AND CONSENTS CSN: 91047719179 ADMIT DATE:
1. CONSENT TO DIAGNOSTIC TESTS, PROCEDURES, & MEDICALTREATMENT:| voluntarily consent to (and consent on behalf of any child born to
me while hospitalized) care involving routine diagnostic tests, procedures and medical treatment as ordered by my admitting and treating
physicians, including their assistants or designees. In the case of diagnostic studies, | consent to the interpretation of the studies at an off-site
location through the use of telehealth. | consent to medical, nursing, allied health and other students observing and participating in my care
under the supervision of a qualified professional. | consent to photographic recordings or reproducible images during the surgical, medical,
and/or diagnostic procedure(s) and their use for identification, scientific, educational, or research purposes. | also consent to testing for
communicable and blood-borne infectious diseases, such as hepatitis, tuberculosis, and the human immunodeficiency virus (HIV), if a provider
orders testing for diagnostic purposes or if there has been an exposure to healthcare personnel. | have been given no guarantees about the
results that may be obtained from my care.
2. PHYSICIANS AND OTHER HEALTH CARE PROVIDERS WHO ARE NOT EMPLOYEES OF THE HOSPITAL: Physicians and certified registered
nurse anesthetists rendering medical treatment to patients in the hospital are not employed by the Hospital. In most situations, advanced
practitioners, including but not limited to, nurse practitioners, physician assistants, surgical assistants and psychologists, providing
treatment to patients in the Hospital are not employed by the Hospital. You may receive a separate bill for the services of these providers, or
the Hospital bill you receive may have separate charges for services of such providers. Charges for such services are established by the
providers.
3. CONSENT TO USE AND DISCLOSURE OF INFORMATION: |authorize the Hospital and the health care providers on its medical staff to use
and disclose information about me to carry out treatment, payment and healthcare operations. Examples of such uses and disclosures
include, but are not limited to, providing information to: (a) any person, company, or entity (Such as HMOs, insurance companies, workers’
compensation carriers, my employer, the Medicare and Medicaid programs and their intermediaries and review organizations, and any
other payor or its review organization or third party administrator) that is or may be liable for paying any claim for benefits arising out of
services provided to me on an inpatient or outpatient basis, or for any ambulance services provided for my transport to or from the Hospital;
(b) any health care provider or ambulance company providing services for me; (c) any providers who may be providing follow-up care to me
after discharge such as home health agencies, nursing homes, physicians, and other health care facilities to which the patient may be
transferred; (d) any licensing or accrediting organizations necessary for the Hospital to obtain or maintain licensure or accreditation; (e) to
providers or entities for the purposes of conducting medical audits, utilization reviews, or quality assurance reviews; and (f) any other
persons or entities described in the Hospital’s Notice of Privacy Practices. This consent includes the release of medical records and billing
information related to drug-related conditions, alcoholism, psychological and psychiatric conditions, and/or communicable or blood-borne
infectious diseases, such as hepatitis, tuberculosis, and the human immunodeficiency virus (HIV). | also consent to any third party payor or
its review organization paying for my care to discuss my plan of treatment for utilization review purposes. | also authorize the release of my
social security number to the manufacturer of any implanted medical device in accordance with the Medical Device Tracking Act.
4. FINANCIAL AGREEMENT ANDASSIGNMENT OF BENEFITS:| agree that | am responsible for payment of my Hospital bill. Payment of any
portion of my bill not covered by a third party payor is due upon discharge from the Hospital unless the Hospital has agreed to other
arrangements. | agree to the assignment of all third party payor benefits to the Hospital and to any health care provider rendering services to
me. | agree to pay the Hospital and other health care providers for all charges for services that are not covered or paid by any third party
payor regardless of the reason, including but not limited to a determination by any third party payor that such services are not covered
services or medically necessary. To the extent | am a Medicare or Medicaid beneficiary, | certify that any information | provide in applying for
payment under Title XVIII (Medicare) or Title XIX (Medicaid) of the Social Security Act is correct. | request payment of authorized benefits to be
made on my behalf to Baptist Health facility or to any health care provider rendering services to me by the Medicare or Medicaid program. |
hereby irrevocably appoint Hospital as my authorized representative to pursue any claims, penalties, and administrative and/or legal
remedies on my behalf for collection against any responsible payer, employer-sponsored medical benefit plans, third party liability carrier or,
any other responsible third party for any and all benefits due me for the payment of charges associated with my treatment. This assignment
shall not be construed as an obligation of the Hospital to pursue any such right of recovery. | agree to take all actions necessary to assist
Hospital in collecting payment from any such third party payer. | understand that after reasonable notice, any unpaid account may be turned
over to a collection agency and/or attorney for collection. Should it be necessary for the Hospital to pursue collection, | agree to pay all
reasonable collection costs, including

5. OUTPATIENT MEDICARE PATIENTS: Medicare does not cover prescription drugs with only a few exceptions. According to Medicare
regulations, | acknowledge that | am responsible for any drugs furnished to me while an outpatient that meet Medicare’s definition of a
prescription drug. These drugs are also referred to as self-administered but they may be administered to me by Hospital personnel.
Medicare requires Hospital to bill Medicare patients or other third party payers for these drugs. Medicare Part D beneficiaries may submit a
paper claim to the Medicare Part D Plan for possible reimbursement of these drugs in accordance with Medicare Drug Plan enrollment
materials.
6. HOSPITAL IS NOT RESPONSIBLE FOR LOSS OF PERSONAL ARTICLES: | UNDERSTAND THAT THE HOSPITAL MAINTAINS A SAFE FOR

7. SMOKE-FREE ENVIRONMENT: This Hospital maintains a smoke-free environment on its campus. Smoking is prohibited by health care

understand that if | leave my treatment area, | will not be under nursing or medical supervision, and further understand that leaving my
treatment area may complicate or interfere with the course of treatment prescribed by my physician.

[DOB-421] - Admission (Discharged) in BAPTIST HEALTH CORBIN WOMENS HEALTH (continued)
More Information
Vaginal Hysterectomy, Care After
Refer to this sheet in the next few weeks. These instructions provide you with information about caring for yourself 
after your procedure. Your health care provider may also give you more specific instructions. Your treatment has been 
planned according to current medical practices, but problems sometimes occur. Call your health care provider if you 
have any problems or questions after your procedure.
What can I expect after the procedure?
After the procedure, it is common to have: · Pain. · Soreness and numbness in your incision areas. · Vaginal bleeding and discharge. · Constipation. · Temporary problems emptying the bladder. · Feelings of sadness or other emotions.
Follow these instructions at home:
Medicines
· Take over-the-counter and prescription medicines only as told by your health care provider. · If you were prescribed an antibiotic medicine, take it as told by your health care provider. Do not stop taking the 
antibiotic even if you start to feel better. · Do not drive or operate heavy machinery while taking prescription pain medicine.
Activity
· Return to your normal activities as told by your health care provider. Ask your health care provider what 
activities are safe for you. · Get regular exercise as told by your health care provider. You may be told to take short walks every day and go 
farther each time. · Do not lift anything that is heavier than 10 lb (4.5 kg).
General instructions
· Do not put anything in your vagina for 6 weeks after your surgery or as told by 
your health care provider. This includes tampons and douches. · Do not have sex until your health care provider says you can. · Do not take baths, swim, or use a hot tub until your health care provider 
approves. · Drink enough fluid to keep your urine clear or pale yellow. · Do not drive for 24 hours if you were given a sedative. · Keep all follow-up visits as told by your health care provider. This is important.

[DOB-423] - Admission (Discharged) in BAPTIST HEALTH CORBIN WOMENS HEALTH (continued)
More Information (continued)
Contact a health care provider if:
· Your pain medicine is not helping. · You have a fever. · You have redness, swelling, or pain at your incision site. · You have blood, pus, or a bad-smelling discharge from your vagina. · You continue to have difficulty urinating.
Get help right away if:
· You have severe abdominal or back pain. · You have heavy bleeding from your vagina. · You have chest pain or shortness of breath.
This information is not intended to replace advice given to you by your health care provider. Make sure you discuss 
any questions you have with your health care provider.

Urethral Vaginal Sling, Care After
Refer to this sheet in the next few weeks. These instructions provide you with information on caring for yourself after 
your procedure. Your health care provider may also give you more specific instructions. Your treatment has been 
planned according to current medical practices, but problems sometimes occur. Call your health care provider if you 
have any problems or questions after your procedure.
What can I expect after the procedure?
After your procedure, it is typical to have the following: · A catheter in your bladder until your bladder is able to work on its own properly. You will be instructed on how 
to empty the catheter bag. · Absorbable stitches in your incisions. They will slowly dissolve over 1–2 months. Follow these instructions at home:
· Get plenty of rest. · Only take over-the-counter or prescription medicines as directed by your health care provider. Do not take 
aspirin because it can cause bleeding. · Do not take baths. Take showers until your health care provider tells you otherwise. · You may resume your usual diet. Eat a well-balanced diet. · Drink enough fluids to keep your urine clear or pale yellow. · Limit exercise and activities as directed by your health care provider. Do not lift anything heavier than 5 pounds 
(2.3 kg). · Do not douche, use tampons, or have sexual intercourse for 6 weeks after your procedure. · Follow up with your health care provider as directed.
Contact a health care provider if:
· You have a heavy or bad smelling vaginal discharge. · You have a rash. · You have pain that is not controlled with medicines. · You have lightheadedness or feel faint.
Get help right away if:
· You have a fever. · You have vaginal bleeding. · You faint. · You have shortness of breath. · You have chest, abdominal, or leg pain. · You have pain when urinating or cannot urinate. · Your catheter is still in your bladder and becomes blocked. · You have swelling, redness, and pain in the vaginal area.
This information is not intended to replace advice given to you by your health care provider. Make sure you discuss

Ibuprofen tablets and capsules
What is this medicine?
IBUPROFEN (eye BYOO proe fen) is a non-steroidal anti-inflammatory drug (NSAID). It is used for dental pain, 
fever, headaches or migraines, osteoarthritis, rheumatoid arthritis, or painful monthly periods. It can also relieve minor 
aches and pains caused by a cold, flu, or sore throat.
This medicine may be used for other purposes; ask your health care provider or pharmacist if you have questions.
COMMON BRAND NAME(S): Advil, Advil Junior Strength, Advil Migraine, Genpril, Ibren, IBU, Midol, Midol 
Cramps and Body Aches, Motrin, Motrin IB, Motrin Junior Strength, Motrin Migraine Pain, Samson-8, Toxicology 
Saliva Collection
What should I tell my health care provider before I take this medicine?
They need to know if you have any of these conditions:
-asthma
-cigarette smoker
-drink more than 3 alcohol containing drinks a day
-heart disease or circulation problems such as heart failure or leg edema (fluid retention)
-high blood pressure
-kidney disease
-liver disease
-stomach bleeding or ulcers
-an unusual or allergic reaction to ibuprofen, aspirin, other NSAIDS, other medicines, foods, dyes, or preservatives
-pregnant or trying to get pregnant
-breast-feeding
How should I use this medicine?

[DOB-437] - Admission (Discharged) in BAPTIST HEALTH CORBIN WOMENS HEALTH (continued)
More Information (continued)
Take this medicine by mouth with a glass of water. Follow the directions on the prescription label. Take this medicine 
with food if your stomach gets upset. Try to not lie down for at least 10 minutes after you take the medicine. Take your 
medicine at regular intervals. Do not take your medicine more often than directed.
A special MedGuide will be given to you by the pharmacist with each prescription and refill. Be sure to read this 
information carefully each time.
Talk to your pediatrician regarding the use of this medicine in children. Special care may be needed.
Overdosage: If you think you have taken too much of this medicine contact a poison control center or emergency room 
at once.
NOTE: This medicine is only for you. Do not share this medicine with others.
What if I miss a dose?
If you miss a dose, take it as soon as you can. If it is almost time for your next dose, take only that dose. Do not take 
double or extra doses.
What may interact with this medicine?
Do not take this medicine with any of the following medications:
-cidofovir
-ketorolac
-methotrexate
-pemetrexed
This medicine may also interact with the following medications:
-alcohol
-aspirin
-diuretics
-lithium
-other drugs for inflammation like prednisone

MRN: [PHONE-438], DOB: [DOB-459], Sex: F

[DOB-439] - Admission (Discharged) in BAPTIST HEALTH CORBIN WOMENS HEALTH (continued)

-warfarin
This list may not describe all possible interactions. Give your health care provider a list of all the medicines, herbs, 
non-prescription drugs, or dietary supplements you use. Also tell them if you smoke, drink alcohol, or use illegal drugs. 
Some items may interact with your medicine.
What should I watch for while using this medicine?
Tell your doctor or healthcare professional if your symptoms do not start to get better or if they get worse.
This medicine does not prevent heart attack or stroke. In fact, this medicine may increase the chance of a heart attack or 
stroke. The chance may increase with longer use of this medicine and in people who have heart disease. If you take 
aspirin to prevent heart attack or stroke, talk with your doctor or health care professional.
Do not take other medicines that contain aspirin, ibuprofen, or naproxen with this medicine. Side effects such as 
stomach upset, nausea, or ulcers may be more likely to occur. Many medicines available without a prescription should 
not be taken with this medicine.
This medicine can cause ulcers and bleeding in the stomach and intestines at any time during treatment. Ulcers and 
bleeding can happen without warning symptoms and can cause death. To reduce your risk, do not smoke cigarettes or 
drink alcohol while you are taking this medicine.
You may get drowsy or dizzy. Do not drive, use machinery, or do anything that needs mental alertness until you know 
how this medicine affects you. Do not stand or sit up quickly, especially if you are an older patient. This reduces the 
risk of dizzy or fainting spells.
This medicine can cause you to bleed more easily. Try to avoid damage to your teeth and gums when you brush or floss 
your teeth.
This medicine may be used to treat migraines. If you take migraine medicines for 10 or more days a month, your 
migraines may get worse. Keep a diary of headache days and medicine use. Contact your healthcare professional if 
your migraine attacks occur more frequently.
What side effects may I notice from receiving this medicine?
Side effects that you should report to your doctor or health care professional as soon as possible:
-allergic reactions like skin rash, itching or hives, swelling of the face, lips, or tongue
-severe stomach pain
-signs and symptoms of bleeding such as bloody or black, tarry stools; red or dark-brown urine; spitting up blood or 
brown material that looks like coffee grounds; red spots on the skin; unusual bruising or bleeding from the eye, gums,

Docusate capsules
What is this medicine?
DOCUSATE (doc CUE sayt) is stool softener. It helps prevent constipation and straining or discomfort associated with 
hard or dry stools.
This medicine may be used for other purposes; ask your health care provider or pharmacist if you have questions.
COMMON BRAND NAME(S): Colace, Colace Clear, Correctol, D.O.S., DC, Doc-Q-Lace, DocuLace, Docusoft S, DOK, DOK Extra Strength, Dulcolax, Genasoft, Kao-Tin, Kaopectate Liqui-Gels, Phillips Stool Softener, Stool 
Softener, Stool Softner DC, Sulfolax, Sur-Q-Lax, Surfak, Uni-Ease
What should I tell my health care provider before I take this medicine?
They need to know if you have any of these conditions:
-nausea or vomiting
-severe constipation
-stomach pain
-sudden change in bowel habit lasting more than 2 weeks
-an unusual or allergic reaction to docusate, other medicines, foods, dyes, or preservatives
-pregnant or trying to get pregnant
-breast-feeding
How should I use this medicine?
Take this medicine by mouth with a glass of water. Follow the directions on the label. Take your doses at regular 
intervals. Do not take your medicine more often than directed.
Talk to your pediatrician regarding the use of this medicine in children. While this medicine may be prescribed for 
children as young as 2 years for selected conditions, precautions do apply.
Overdosage: If you think you have taken too much of this medicine contact a poison control center or emergency room 
at once.

moderate to severe pain.

-Crohn's disease, inflammatory bowel disease, or ulcerative colitis
-drug abuse or addiction
-head injury
-heart or circulation problems
-if you often drink alcohol
-kidney disease or problems going to the bathroom
-liver disease
-lung disease, asthma, or breathing problems
-an unusual or allergic reaction to acetaminophen, oxycodone, other opioid analgesics, other medicines, foods, dyes, or 
preservatives
-pregnant or trying to get pregnant
-breast-feeding

the medication for pain relief. Tolerance is normal and is expected if you take this medicine for a long time.
Do not suddenly stop taking your medicine because you may develop a severe reaction. Your body becomes used to the 
medicine. This does NOT mean you are addicted. Addiction is a behavior related to getting and using a drug for a nonmedical reason. If you have pain, you have a medical reason to take pain medicine. Your doctor will tell you how much 
medicine to take. If your doctor wants you to stop the medicine, the dose will be slowly lowered over time to avoid any 
side effects.
There are different types of narcotic medicines (opiates). If you take more than one type at the same time or if you are 
taking another medicine that also causes drowsiness, you may have more side effects. Give your health care provider a 
list of all medicines you use. Your doctor will tell you how much medicine to take. Do not take more medicine than 
directed. Call emergency for help if you have problems breathing or unusual sleepiness.
Do not take other medicines that contain acetaminophen with this medicine. Always read labels carefully. If you have 
questions, ask your doctor or pharmacist.
If you take too much acetaminophen get medical help right away. Too much acetaminophen can be very dangerous and 
cause liver damage. Even if you do not have symptoms, it is important to get help right away.
You may get drowsy or dizzy. Do not drive, use machinery, or do anything that needs mental alertness until you know 
how this medicine affects you. Do not stand or sit up quickly, especially if you are an older patient. This reduces the 
risk of dizzy or fainting spells. Alcohol may interfere with the effect of this medicine. Avoid alcoholic drinks.
The medicine will cause constipation. Try to have a bowel movement at least every 2 to 3 days. If you do not have a 
bowel movement for 3 days, call your doctor or health care professional.
Your mouth may get dry. Chewing sugarless gum or sucking hard candy, and drinking plenty or water may help. 
Contact your doctor if the problem does not go away or is severe.
What side effects may I notice from receiving this medicine?
Side effects that you should report to your doctor or health care professional as soon as possible:
-allergic reactions like skin rash, itching or hives, swelling of the face, lips, or tongue
-breathing problems
-confusion
-redness, blistering, peeling or loosening of the skin, including inside the mouth
-signs and symptoms of liver injury like dark yellow or brown urine; general ill feeling or flu-like symptoms; lightcolored stools; loss of appetite; nausea; right upper belly pain; unusually weak or tired; yellowing of the eyes or skin

Where should I keep my medicine?
Keep out of the reach of children. This medicine can be abused. Keep your medicine in a safe place to protect it from 
theft. Do not share this medicine with anyone. Selling or giving away this medicine is dangerous and against the law.
This medicine may cause accidental overdose and death if it taken by other adults, children, or pets. Mix any unused 
medicine with a substance like cat litter or coffee grounds. Then throw the medicine away in a sealed container like a 
sealed bag or a coffee can with a lid. Do not use the medicine after the expiration date.
Store at room temperature between 20 and 25 degrees C (68 and 77 degrees F). NOTE: This sheet is a summary. It may not cover all possible information. If you have questions about this medicine, 
talk to your doctor, pharmacist, or health care provider.

PREVENTING SURGICAL SITE INFECTIONS
· Call 911 or have someone take you to the Emergency Department if you have any of the following: · Sudden numbness or weakness of your face, arm or leg especially on one side of the body
· Sudden confusion, difficulty speaking or trouble understanding
· Changes in your vision or loss of sight in one eye
· Sudden severe headache with no known cause
· Sudden dizziness, trouble walking, loss of balance or coordination
